      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Tanzania" title="Politics of Tanzania">Politics of Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Tanzania" title="Constitution of Tanzania">Constitution of Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Tanzania is a <a href="/wiki/One_party_dominant_state" class="mw-redirect" title="One party dominant state">one party dominant state</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Chama_Cha_Mapinduzi" title="Chama Cha Mapinduzi">Chama Cha Mapinduzi</a> (CCM) party in power. From its formation until 1992, it was the only legally permitted party in the country. This changed on 1 July 1992, when the constitution was amended.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 3</span></sup> Chama cha Mapinduzi (CCM) has held power since independence in 1961. It is the longest-serving ruling party in Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-cfr.org_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cfr.org-68">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/John_Magufuli" title="John Magufuli">John Magufuli</a> won the October 2015 presidential election and secured a two-thirds majority in parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[90]</a></sup> The main opposition party in Tanzania since multiparty politics in 1992 is called <a href="/wiki/Chadema" title="Chadema">Chama cha Demokrasia na Maendeleo (Chadema)</a> (<a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">Swahili</a> for "Party for Democracy and Progress"). The leader of Chadema party is <a href="/wiki/Freeman_Mbowe" title="Freeman Mbowe">Freeman Mbowe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Zanzibar, the country's semi-autonomous state, <a href="/wiki/Alliance_for_Change_and_Transparency" title="Alliance for Change and Transparency">The Alliance for Change and Transparency-Wazalendois</a> (ACT-Wazalendo) is considered the main opposition political party. The constitution of Zanzibar requires the party that comes in second in the polls to join a coalition with the winning party. ACT-Wazalendo joined a coalition government with the islands’ ruling party Chama Cha Mapinduzi in December 2020 after Zanzibar disputed <a href="/wiki/2020_Zanzibari_general_election" title="2020 Zanzibari general election">elections</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In November 2020, Magufuli once again was declared the winner for his second term as president. Election fraud was suspected. The national electoral commission announced that Magufuli received 84%, or about 12.5 million votes and the top opposition candidate, <a href="/wiki/Tundu_Lissu" title="Tundu Lissu">Tundu Lissu</a> received 13%, about 1.9&nbsp;million votes.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[93]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In March 2021, it was announced that Magufuli had died whilst serving in office, meaning that his vice president, <a href="/wiki/Samia_Suluhu_Hassan" title="Samia Suluhu Hassan">Samia Suluhu Hassan</a>, became the country's president.<sup id="cite_ref-:7_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-71">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive">Executive</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Executive">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:298px;max-width:298px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Dr_Philip_Mpango.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Dr_Philip_Mpango.jpg/150px-Dr_Philip_Mpango.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="150" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Dr_Philip_Mpango.jpg/225px-Dr_Philip_Mpango.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/79/Dr_Philip_Mpango.jpg 2x" data-file-width="270" data-file-height="270"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dr._Philip_Mpango&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dr. Philip Mpango (page does not exist)">Vice-President Dr. Philip Mpango</a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:142px;max-width:142px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg/140px-Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg" decoding="async" width="140" height="190" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg/210px-Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg/280px-Kassim_Majaliwa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1333" data-file-height="1805"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption text-align-center">
           <a href="/wiki/Kassim_Majaliwa" title="Kassim Majaliwa">Prime Minister Kassim Majaliwa</a>
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/President_of_Tanzania" title="President of Tanzania">president of Tanzania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Tanzania_National_Assembly_members" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Tanzania National Assembly members">members of the National Assembly</a> are elected concurrently by direct popular vote for five-year terms.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 42(2)</span></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_Tanzania" class="mw-redirect" title="Vice President of Tanzania">vice-president</a> is elected for a five-year term at the same time as the president and on the same ticket.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§§ 47(2), 50(1)</span></sup> Neither the president nor the vice-president may be a member of the National Assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 66(2)</span></sup> The president appoints a <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Tanzania" title="Prime Minister of Tanzania">prime minister</a>, subject to confirmation by the assembly, to serve as the government's leader in the assembly.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§§ 51(1)-(2), 52(2)</span></sup> The president selects his or her <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Tanzania" title="Cabinet of Tanzania">cabinet</a> from assembly members.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 55</span></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislature">Legislature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Legislature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>All <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a> power relating to mainland Tanzania and union matters is vested in the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Tanzania" class="mw-redirect" title="National Assembly of Tanzania">National Assembly</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 64(1)</span></sup> which is unicameral and has a maximum of 357 members.<sup id="cite_ref-Edge_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edge-96">[94]</a></sup> These include members elected to represent constituencies, the attorney general, five members elected by the <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> house of representatives from among its own members, the special women's seats that constitute at least 30% of the seats that any party has in the assembly, the speaker of the assembly (if not otherwise a member of the assembly), and the persons (not more than ten) appointed by the president.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 66(1)</span></sup> The Tanzania Electoral Commission demarcates the mainland into constituencies in the number determined by the commission with the consent of the president.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 75</span></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judiciary">Judiciary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Judiciary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Tanzania" title="Chief Justice of Tanzania">Chief Justice of Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Tanzania's legal system is based on English <a href="/wiki/Common_law" title="Common law">common law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tanzania has a four-level judiciary.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> The lowest-level courts on the Tanzanian mainland are the Primary Courts.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> In Zanzibar, the lowest-level courts are the Kadhi's Courts for Islamic family matters and the Primary Courts for all other cases.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> On the mainland, appeal is to either the District Courts or the Resident Magistrates Courts.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> In Zanzibar, appeal is to the Kadhi's Appeal Courts for Islamic family matters and the Magistrates Courts for all other cases.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> From there, appeal is to the <a href="/wiki/High_Court_of_Tanzania" title="High Court of Tanzania">High Court of Mainland Tanzania or Zanzibar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> No appeal regarding Islamic family matters can be made from the High Court of Zanzibar.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 99(1)</span></sup> Otherwise, the final appeal is to the Court of Appeal of Tanzania.<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The High Court of mainland Tanzania has three divisions – commercial, labour, and land<sup id="cite_ref-TZ_court_system_97-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TZ_court_system-97">[95]</a></sup> – and 15 geographic zones.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[97]</a></sup> The High Court of Zanzibar has an industrial division, which hears only labour disputes.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[98]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Mainland and union judges are appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Tanzania" title="Chief Justice of Tanzania">Chief Justice of Tanzania</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[99]</a></sup> except for those of the <a href="/wiki/Appellate_court" title="Appellate court">Court of Appeal</a> and the High Court, who are appointed by the president of Tanzania.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§§ 109(1), 118(2)–(3)</span></sup> </p>
      <p>Tanzania is a party to the <a href="/wiki/Rome_Statute_of_the_International_Criminal_Court" title="Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court">Rome Statute of the International Criminal Court</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Zanzibar">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Spice_Islands_(Zanzibar_highlighted)_sv.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg/220px-Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="271" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg/330px-Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg/440px-Spice_Islands_%28Zanzibar_highlighted%29_sv.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="713" data-file-height="879"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Spice_Islands_(Zanzibar_highlighted)_sv.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The semi-autonomous <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar_Archipelago" title="Zanzibar Archipelago">Zanzibar Archipelago</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The legislative authority in Zanzibar over all non-union matters is vested in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_(Zanzibar)" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Representatives (Zanzibar)">House of Representatives</a> (per the Tanzania constitution)<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 106(3)</span></sup> or the Legislative Council (per the Zanzibar constitution). </p>
      <p>The Legislative Council has two parts: the president of Zanzibar and the House of Representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution_90-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution-90">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 107(1)-(2)</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 63(1)</span></sup> The president is Zanzibar's head of government and the chairman of the Revolutionary Council, in which the executive authority of Zanzibar is invested.<sup id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_98-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§§ 5A(2), 26(1)</span></sup> Zanzibar has two vice-presidents, with the first being from the main opposition party in the house.<sup id="cite_ref-Eisa_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa-103">[101]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Troubled_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Troubled-104">[102]</a></sup> The second is from the party in power and is the leader of government business in the House.<sup id="cite_ref-Troubled_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Troubled-104">[102]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The president and the members of the House of Representatives have five-year terms and can be elected for a second term.<sup id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_98-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 28(2)</span></sup> </p>
      <p>The president selects ministers from members of the House of Representatives,<sup id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_98-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 42(2)</span></sup> with the ministers allocated according to the number of House seats won by political parties.<sup id="cite_ref-Eisa_103-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa-103">[101]</a></sup> The Revolutionary Council consists of the president, both vice-presidents, all ministers, the <a href="/wiki/Attorney_general" title="Attorney general">attorney general</a> of Zanzibar, and other house members deemed fit by the president.<sup id="cite_ref-Eisa_103-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eisa-103">[101]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The House of Representatives is composed of elected members, ten members appointed by the president, all the regional commissioners of Zanzibar, the attorney general, and appointed female members whose number must be equal to 30 per cent of the elected members.<sup id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_98-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§§ 55(3), 64, 67(1)</span></sup> The House determines the number of its elected members<sup id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_98-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 120(2)</span></sup> with the Zanzibar Electoral Commission determining the boundaries of each election constituency.<sup id="cite_ref-Zanzibar_Constitution_98-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Zanzibar_Constitution-98">[96]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>§ 120(1)</span></sup> In 2013, the House had 81 members: fifty elected members, five regional commissioners, the attorney general, ten members appointed by the president, and fifteen appointed female members.<sup id="cite_ref-Edge_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Edge-96">[94]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_subdivisions">Administrative subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Administrative subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Tanzania" title="Regions of Tanzania">Regions of Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Tanzania" title="Districts of Tanzania">Districts of Tanzania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Subdivisions_of_Tanzania" title="Subdivisions of Tanzania">Subdivisions of Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tanzania,_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_(%2Bdetails).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg/220px-Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg/330px-Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg/440px-Tanzania%2C_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_%28%2Bdetails%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="3096" data-file-height="2947"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tanzania,_administrative_divisions_-_de_-_colored_(%2Bdetails).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Regions of Tanzania
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1972, local government on the mainland was abolished and replaced with direct rule from the central government. Local government, however, was reintroduced in the beginning of the 1980s, when the rural councils and rural authorities were re-established. Local government elections took place in 1983, and functioning councils started in 1984. In 1999, a Local Government Reform Programme was enacted by the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Tanzania)" title="National Assembly (Tanzania)">National Assembly</a>, setting "a comprehensive and ambitious agenda ... [covering] four areas: political decentralization, financial decentralization, administrative decentralization and changed central-local relations, with the mainland government having overriding powers within the framework of the Constitution."<sup id="cite_ref-Kunnat_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kunnat-105">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2016, Tanzania is divided into thirty-one <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_Tanzania" title="Regions of Tanzania">regions</a> (<i>mkoa</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[104]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[105]</a></sup> twenty-six on the mainland and five in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a> (three on <a href="/wiki/Unguja" title="Unguja">Unguja</a>, two on <a href="/wiki/Pemba,_Tanzania" class="mw-redirect" title="Pemba, Tanzania">Pemba</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[106]</a></sup> In 2012, the thirty former regions were divided into 169 <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Tanzania" title="Districts of Tanzania">districts</a> (wilaya), also known as local government authorities. Of those districts, 34 were urban units, which were further classified as three city councils (<a href="/wiki/Arusha" title="Arusha">Arusha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbeya" title="Mbeya">Mbeya</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mwanza" title="Mwanza">Mwanza</a>), nineteen municipal councils, and twelve town councils.<sup id="cite_ref-2012_census_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2012_census-8">[8]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The urban units have an autonomous city, municipal, or town council and are subdivided into wards and <i>mtaa</i>. The non-urban units have an autonomous district council but are subdivided into village councils or township authorities (first level) and then into <i>vitongoji</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Kunnat_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kunnat-105">[103]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The city of Dar es Salaam is unique because it has a city council whose area of jurisdiction overlaps three municipal councils. The mayor of the city council is elected by that council. The twenty-member city council is composed of eleven persons elected by the municipal councils, seven members of the National Assembly, and "Nominated members of parliament under 'Special Seats' for women". Each municipal council also has a mayor. "The City Council performs a coordinating role and attends to issues cutting across the three municipalities", including security and emergency services.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[107]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[108]</a></sup> The city of Mwanza has a city council whose areal jurisdiction overlaps two municipal councils. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Tanzania" title="Foreign relations of Tanzania">Foreign relations of Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bilateral_relations">Bilateral relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Bilateral relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_with_Jaka_Mwambi.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Dmitry_Medvedev_with_Jaka_Mwambi.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_with_Jaka_Mwambi.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Dmitry_Medvedev_with_Jaka_Mwambi.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_with_Jaka_Mwambi.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Dmitry_Medvedev_with_Jaka_Mwambi.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_with_Jaka_Mwambi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="334"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_with_Jaka_Mwambi.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tanzanian ambassador to Russia <a href="/wiki/Jaka_Mwambi" title="Jaka Mwambi">Jaka Mwambi</a> presenting his credentials to the Russian President <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">Dmitry Medvedev</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG/170px-Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG" decoding="async" width="170" height="285" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG/255px-Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG/340px-Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2388" data-file-height="4000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tanzanian_Embassy_Washington.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Embassy_of_Tanzania,_Washington,_D.C." title="Embassy of Tanzania, Washington, D.C.">Tanzanian Embassy</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_End,_Washington,_D.C." class="mw-redirect" title="West End, Washington, D.C.">West End</a>, Washington, D.C., USA
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Apart from its border dispute with Malawi, Tanzania had cordial relations with its neighbours in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-year_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-year-111">[109]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Malawi%E2%80%93Tanzania_relations" title="Malawi–Tanzania relations">Relations between Tanzania and Malawi</a> have been tense because of a <a href="/wiki/Lake_Malawi#Tanzania–Malawi_dispute" title="Lake Malawi">dispute</a> over the countries' <a href="/wiki/Lake_Nyasa" class="mw-redirect" title="Lake Nyasa">Lake Nyasa</a> (Lake Malawi) border. An unsuccessful mediation regarding this issue took place in March 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-frame_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frame-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-year_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-year-111">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AllAfrica.com_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AllAfrica.com-112">[110]</a></sup> The two countries agreed in 2013 to ask the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> (ICJ) to resolve the dispute should mediation be unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-tvcnews.tv_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tvcnews.tv-113">[111]</a></sup> Malawi, but not Tanzania, has accepted the compulsory jurisdiction of the ICJ.<sup id="cite_ref-icj-cij.org_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icj-cij.org-114">[112]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rwanda%E2%80%93Tanzania_relations" title="Rwanda–Tanzania relations">Relations between Tanzania and Rwanda</a> deteriorated in 2013 when Tanzanian President <a href="/wiki/Jakaya_Kikwete" title="Jakaya Kikwete">Jakaya Kikwete</a> said that if the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DRC) could negotiate with some of its enemies, Rwanda should be able to do the same.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[113]</a></sup> Rwandan President <a href="/wiki/Paul_Kagame" title="Paul Kagame">Paul Kagame</a> then expressed "contempt" for Kikwete's statement.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[114]</a></sup> The tension was renewed in May 2014 when, in a speech to the Tanzanian <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Tanzania)" title="National Assembly (Tanzania)">National Assembly</a>, Foreign Affairs Minister <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Membe" title="Bernard Membe">Bernard Membe</a> renewed his claim that Rwandans were causing instability in the DRC. Rwandan Foreign Affairs Minister <a href="/wiki/Louise_Mushikiwabo" title="Louise Mushikiwabo">Louise Mushikiwabo</a> responded, "As for Tanzania's foreign minister whose anti-Rwanda rant in parliament I heard, he would benefit from a lesson in the history of the region."<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tanzania has maintained strong <a href="/wiki/Tanzania-United_Kingdom_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanzania-United Kingdom relations">relations</a> with the United Kingdom since its independence; Britain remains the largest non-African importer of Tanzanian tea<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[116]</a></sup> and other raw materials are exchanged. Britain remains a high contributor of tourists to Tanzania. Both are members of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> and engage in strategic union in defence, security and ceremonial affairs; the Tanzanian <a href="/wiki/High_Commission_of_Tanzania,_London" title="High Commission of Tanzania, London">High Commission</a> is in London and the British have a <a href="/wiki/British_High_Commission,_Dar_es_Salaam" title="British High Commission, Dar es Salaam">High Commission</a> in Dar es Salaam. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tanzania%E2%80%93China_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanzania–China relations">Tanzania–China relations</a> have strengthened in recent years as trade between the two countries and Chinese investment in Tanzanian infrastructure have increased rapidly.<sup id="cite_ref-frame_74-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frame-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tanzania%E2%80%93United_States_relations" title="Tanzania–United States relations">Relations with the United States</a> are warm, with President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_presidential_trips_made_by_Barack_Obama" title="List of presidential trips made by Barack Obama">visiting Tanzania</a> in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-cnn_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn-121">[119]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tanzania's relations with other donor countries, including Japan and members of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, are generally good, though donors are concerned about Tanzania's commitment to reducing government corruption.<sup id="cite_ref-frame_74-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frame-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-year_111-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-year-111">[109]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Multilateral_relations">Multilateral relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Multilateral relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>Tanzania is a member of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC), along with Uganda, Kenya, Rwanda,Burundi and South Sudan.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[120]</a></sup> According to the East African Common Market Protocol of 2010, the free trade and free movement of people is guaranteed, including the right to reside in another member country for purposes of employment.<sup id="cite_ref-frame_74-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frame-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>1250</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[122]</a></sup> This protocol, however, has not been implemented because of work permit and other bureaucratic, legal, and financial obstacles.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[123]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tanzania is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a> (SADC).<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[124]</a></sup> The EAC, the SADC, and the <a href="/wiki/Common_Market_for_Eastern_and_Southern_Africa" title="Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa">Common Market for Eastern and Southern Africa</a> agreed in June 2011 to negotiate the creation of a Tripartite Free Trade Area spanning 26 African countries, with a goal to complete the first phase of negotiations within 36 months.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 31 October 2014, Tanzania was contributing 2,253 soldiers and other personnel to various United Nations peacekeeping operations.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[126]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_People%27s_Defence_Force" title="Tanzania People's Defence Force">Tanzanian military</a> is participating along with South African and Malawian militaries in the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Force_Intervention_Brigade" title="United Nations Force Intervention Brigade">United Nations Force Intervention Brigade</a> (MONUSCO) in the Democratic Republic of the Congo (DRC). The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> authorised the force on 28 March 2013 to conduct targeted offensive operations to neutralise groups that threaten peace in the DRC.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[127]</a></sup> Tanzania was also participating in peacekeeping missions in the <a href="/wiki/Darfur" title="Darfur">Darfur</a> Region of Sudan (<a href="/wiki/UNAMID" class="mw-redirect" title="UNAMID">UNAMID</a>); <a href="/wiki/Abyei" title="Abyei">Abyei</a>, control of which is contested between South Sudan and Sudan (<a href="/wiki/UNISFA" class="mw-redirect" title="UNISFA">UNISFA</a>); the Central African Republic (MINUSCA); Lebanon (<a href="/wiki/UNIFIL" class="mw-redirect" title="UNIFIL">UNIFIL</a>); and South Sudan (<a href="/wiki/UNMISS" class="mw-redirect" title="UNMISS">UNMISS</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[128]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2019, Tanzania signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[129]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:FIB-training-22_(9311333487).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg/220px-FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg/330px-FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg/440px-FIB-training-22_%289311333487%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="834"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:FIB-training-22_(9311333487).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>FIB Tanzanian special forces during training
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Tanzania" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Tanzania">Military of Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_People%27s_Defence_Force" title="Tanzania People's Defence Force">Tanzania People's Defence Force</a> (TPDF) (Kiswahili: Jeshi la Wananchi wa Tanzania (JWTZ)) is the armed forces of Tanzania, operating as a people's force under civilian control. It is composed of five branches or commands: Land Force (army), Air Force, Naval Command, National Service, Headquarter (MMJ).<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[130]</a></sup> Tanzanian citizens are able to volunteer for military service from 15 years of age, and 18 years of age for compulsory military service upon graduation from secondary school. Conscript service obligation was 2 years as of 2004. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Tanzania" title="Human rights in Tanzania">Human rights in Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_people_with_albinism" title="Persecution of people with albinism">Persecution of people with albinism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Tanzania" title="LGBT rights in Tanzania">LGBT rights in Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Throughout Tanzania, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_by_country_or_territory" title="LGBT rights by country or territory">sex acts between men</a> are illegal and carry a maximum penalty of life imprisonment.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[131]</a></sup> According to a 2007 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Pew Research Centre">Pew Research Centre</a> survey, 95 per cent of Tanzanians believed that homosexuality should not be accepted by society.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[132]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>People with <a href="/wiki/Albinism" title="Albinism">albinism</a> living in Tanzania are often attacked, killed or mutilated because of superstitions related to the black-magical practice known as <a href="/wiki/Muti" title="Muti">muti</a> that say body parts of albinos have magical properties.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[133]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tanzania has the highest occurrence of this human rights violation among 27 African countries where <a href="/wiki/Muti" title="Muti">muti</a> is known to be practised.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In December 2019, <a href="/wiki/Amnesty_International" title="Amnesty International">Amnesty International</a> reported that the Tanzanian government annulled the right of NGOs as well as individuals to directly file any case against it at the Arusha-based African Court for Human and Peoples' Rights.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[135]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_and_infrastructure">Economy and infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Economy and infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Tanzania" title="Economy of Tanzania">Economy of Tanzania</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poverty_in_Tanzania" title="Poverty in Tanzania">Poverty in Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_Tanzania_before_dusk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bank_of_Tanzania_before_dusk.jpg/220px-Bank_of_Tanzania_before_dusk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bank_of_Tanzania_before_dusk.jpg/330px-Bank_of_Tanzania_before_dusk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Bank_of_Tanzania_before_dusk.jpg/440px-Bank_of_Tanzania_before_dusk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1067"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bank_of_Tanzania_before_dusk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Tanzania" title="Bank of Tanzania">Bank of Tanzania</a> Twin Towers
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, according to the IMF, Tanzania's gross domestic product (GDP) was an estimated $56.7&nbsp;billion (nominal), or $176.5&nbsp;billion on a <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> (PPP) basis. GDP per capita (PPP) was $3,457.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[136]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From 2009 through 2013, Tanzania's per capita GDP (based on constant local currency) grew an average of 3.5% per year, higher than any other member of the <a href="/wiki/East_African_Community" title="East African Community">East African Community</a> (EAC) and exceeded by only nine countries in Sub-Saharan Africa: the Democratic Republic of the Congo, Ethiopia, Ghana, Lesotho, Liberia, Mozambique, Sierra Leone, Zambia, and Zimbabwe.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[137]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tanzania's largest trading partners in 2017 for its US$5.3&nbsp;billion in exports were India, Vietnam, South Africa, Switzerland, and China.<sup id="cite_ref-UND_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UND-140">[138]</a></sup> Its imports totalled US$8.17&nbsp;billion, with India, Switzerland, Saudi Arabia, China, and the United Arab Emirates being the biggest partners.<sup id="cite_ref-UND_140-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UND-140">[138]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG/220px-The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG/330px-The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG/440px-The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_close_view_of_the_Kariakoo_market_in_Dar_es_Salaam.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/Kariakoo" title="Kariakoo">Kariakoo</a> market in Dar es Salaam
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tanzania weathered the <a href="/wiki/Great_Recession" title="Great Recession">Great Recession</a>, which began in late 2008 or early 2009, relatively well. Strong gold prices, bolstering the country's <a href="/wiki/Mining_industry_of_Tanzania" title="Mining industry of Tanzania">mining industry</a>, and Tanzania's poor integration into global markets helped to insulate the country from the downturn.<sup id="cite_ref-frame_74-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frame-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup> Since the recession ended, the Tanzanian economy has expanded rapidly thanks to strong tourism, telecommunications, and banking sectors.<sup id="cite_ref-frame_74-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frame-74">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 1250</span></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a>, however, recent growth in the national economy has benefited only the "very few", leaving out the majority of the population.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[139]</a></sup> Tanzania's 2013 <a href="/wiki/Global_Hunger_Index" title="Global Hunger Index">Global Hunger Index</a> was worse than any other country in the EAC except Burundi.<sup id="cite_ref-GHI_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GHI-142">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 15</span></sup> The proportion of persons who were undernourished in 2010–12 was also worse than any other EAC country except Burundi.<sup id="cite_ref-GHI_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GHI-142">[140]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 51</span></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2020, the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> declared the rise of the Tanzanian economy from low income to lower <a href="/wiki/Middle_income_country" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle income country">middle income country</a>, with a gross domestic product (GDP) estimated to be between US$1,006 and US$3,955.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[141]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[142]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hunger_and_poverty">Hunger and poverty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Hunger and poverty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Tanzania has made some progress towards reducing extreme hunger and malnutrition. The Global Hunger Index ranked the situation as "alarming" with a score of 42 in the year 2000; since then the GHI has declined to 29.5.<sup id="cite_ref-globalhungerindex.org_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalhungerindex.org-145">[143]</a></sup> Children in rural areas suffer substantially higher rates of malnutrition and chronic hunger, although urban-rural disparities have narrowed as regards both stunting and underweight.<sup id="cite_ref-Tanzania_UNDP_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania_UNDP-146">[144]</a></sup> Low rural sector productivity arises mainly from inadequate infrastructure investment; limited access to farm inputs, extension services and credit; limited technology as well as trade and marketing support; and heavy dependence on rain-fed agriculture and natural resources.<sup id="cite_ref-Tanzania_UNDP_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania_UNDP-146">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Approximately 68 per cent of Tanzania's 44.9&nbsp;million citizens live below the poverty line of $1.25 a day. 32 per cent of the population are malnourished.<sup id="cite_ref-globalhungerindex.org_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-globalhungerindex.org-145">[143]</a></sup> The most prominent challenges Tanzania faces in poverty reduction are unsustainable harvesting of its natural resources, unchecked cultivation, climate change and water- source encroachment, according to the United Nations Development Programme (UNDP).<sup id="cite_ref-Tanzania_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania-147">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are very few resources for Tanzanians in terms of credit services, infrastructure or availability to improved agricultural technologies, which further exacerbates hunger and poverty in the country according to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">UNDP.</a><sup id="cite_ref-Tanzania_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania-147">[145]</a></sup> Tanzania ranks 159 out of 187 countries in poverty according to the United Nation's Human Development Index (2014).<sup id="cite_ref-Tanzania_147-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tanzania-147">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The 2019 <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> report showed that in the last 10 years, poverty has reduced by 8 per cent, from 34.4% in 2007 to 26.4% in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[146]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Agriculture">Agriculture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Agriculture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Agriculture_in_Tanzania" title="Agriculture in Tanzania">Agriculture in Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tea_fields,_Tukuyu,_Tanzania.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg/220px-Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg/330px-Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg/440px-Tea_fields%2C_Tukuyu%2C_Tanzania.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tea_fields,_Tukuyu,_Tanzania.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Tea fields in Tukuyu
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Tanzanian economy is heavily based on agriculture, which in 2013 accounted for 24.5 per cent of gross domestic product,<sup id="cite_ref-Abstract_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 37</span></sup> provides 85% of exports,<sup id="cite_ref-factbook_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factbook-19">[17]</a></sup> and accounted for half of the employed workforce;<sup id="cite_ref-Abstract_55-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 56</span></sup> The agricultural sector grew 4.3 per cent in 2012, less than half of the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Development_Goal" class="mw-redirect" title="Millennium Development Goal">Millennium Development Goal</a> target of 10.8%.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[147]</a></sup> 16.4 per cent of the land is <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[148]</a></sup> with 2.4 per cent of the land planted with <a href="/wiki/Permanent_crop" title="Permanent crop">permanent crops</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[149]</a></sup> Tanzania's economy relies on farming, but climate change has impacted their farming. </p>
      <p>Maize was the largest food crop on the Tanzania mainland in 2013 (5.17&nbsp;million tonnes), followed by cassava (1.94&nbsp;million tonnes), sweet potatoes (1.88&nbsp;million tonnes), beans (1.64&nbsp;million tonnes), bananas (1.31&nbsp;million tonnes), rice (1.31&nbsp;million tonnes), and millet (1.04&nbsp;million tonnes).<sup id="cite_ref-Abstract_55-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 58</span></sup> Sugar was the largest <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">cash crop</a> on the mainland in 2013 (296,679 tonnes), followed by cotton (241,198 tonnes), cashew nuts (126,000 tonnes), tobacco (86,877 tonnes), coffee (48,000 tonnes), sisal (37,368 tonnes), and tea (32,422 tonnes).<sup id="cite_ref-Abstract_55-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 58</span></sup> Beef was the largest meat product on the mainland in 2013 (299,581 tonnes), followed by lamb/mutton (115,652 tonnes), chicken (87,408 tonnes), and pork (50,814 tonnes).<sup id="cite_ref-Abstract_55-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abstract-55">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 60</span></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 2002 National Irrigation Master Plan, 29.4&nbsp;million hectares in Tanzania are suitable for irrigation farming; however, only 310,745 hectares were actually being irrigated in June 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[150]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Industry.2C_energy_and_construction"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Industry,_energy_and_construction">Industry, energy and construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Industry, energy and construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Tanzania" title="Energy in Tanzania">Energy in Tanzania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Water_supply_and_sanitation_in_Tanzania" title="Water supply and sanitation in Tanzania">Water supply and sanitation in Tanzania</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource_and_waste_management_in_Tanzania" title="Natural resource and waste management in Tanzania">Natural resource and waste management in Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_companies_of_Tanzania" title="List of companies of Tanzania">List of companies of Tanzania</a>
      </div>
