       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>More than 100 <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Tanzania" title="Languages of Tanzania">languages are spoken in Tanzania</a>, making it the most linguistically diverse country in East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-sim_29-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sim-29">[27]</a></sup> Among the languages spoken are all four of Africa's language families: <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cushitic_languages" title="Cushitic languages">Cushitic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nilotic_languages" title="Nilotic languages">Nilotic</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Khoisan_languages" title="Khoisan languages">Khoisan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sim_29-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sim-29">[27]</a></sup> There are no <i>de jure</i> official languages in Tanzania.<sup id="cite_ref-tzgov_31-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tzgov-31">[29]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Swahili is used in parliamentary debate, in the lower courts, and as a medium of instruction in primary school. English is used in foreign trade, in diplomacy, in higher courts, and as a medium of instruction in secondary and higher education,<sup id="cite_ref-sim_29-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sim-29">[27]</a></sup> The Tanzanian government, however, has plans to discontinue English as a language of instruction.<sup id="cite_ref-afkinsider.com_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afkinsider.com-32">[30]</a></sup> In connection with his Ujamaa social policies, President Nyerere encouraged the use of Swahili to help unify the country's many ethnic groups.<sup id="cite_ref-Joshua_A._Fishman_Distinguished_University_Research_Professor_of_Social_Sciences_Yeshiva_University_Emeritus_2001_361_213-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Joshua_A._Fishman_Distinguished_University_Research_Professor_of_Social_Sciences_Yeshiva_University_Emeritus_2001_361-213">[211]</a></sup> Approximately 10 per cent of Tanzanians speak Swahili as a first language, and up to 90 per cent speak it as a second language.<sup id="cite_ref-sim_29-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sim-29">[27]</a></sup> Many educated Tanzanians are trilingual, also speaking English.<sup id="cite_ref-Quintin_Winks_2011_145_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quintin_Winks_2011_145-214">[212]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bj_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bj-215">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-François_Grosjean_1982_8_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-François_Grosjean_1982_8-216">[214]</a></sup> The widespread use and promotion of Swahili is contributing to the decline of smaller languages in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-sim_29-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sim-29">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Matthias_Brenzinger_1992_86_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Matthias_Brenzinger_1992_86-217">[215]</a></sup> Young children increasingly speak Swahili as a first language, particularly in urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-Elsevier_218-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elsevier-218">[216]</a></sup> Ethnic community languages (ECL) other than Kiswahili are not allowed as a language of instruction. Nor are they taught as a subject, though they might be used unofficially in some cases in initial education. Television and radio programmes in an ECL are prohibited, and it is nearly impossible to get permission to publish a newspaper in an ECL. There is no department of local or regional African Languages and Literatures at the University of Dar es Salaam.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">[217]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> is co-official in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Sandawe_people" title="Sandawe people">Sandawe people</a> speak a language that may be related to the <a href="/wiki/Khoe_languages" title="Khoe languages">Khoe languages</a> of Botswana and Namibia, while the language of the <a href="/wiki/Hadzabe_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadzabe people">Hadzabe people</a>, although it has similar <a href="/wiki/Click_consonant" title="Click consonant">click consonants</a>, is arguably a <a href="/wiki/Language_isolate" title="Language isolate">language isolate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[218]</a></sup> The language of the <a href="/wiki/Iraqw_people" title="Iraqw people">Iraqw people</a> is Cushitic.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[219]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Tanzania" title="Education in Tanzania">Education in Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Nkrumah.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nkrumah.JPG/220px-Nkrumah.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nkrumah.JPG/330px-Nkrumah.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Nkrumah.JPG/440px-Nkrumah.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2576" data-file-height="1932"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Nkrumah.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Nkrumah Hall at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Dar_es_Salaam" title="University of Dar es Salaam">University of Dar es Salaam</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2012, the literacy rate in Tanzania for persons aged 15 and over was estimated to be 67.8 per cent.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[220]</a></sup> Education is compulsory until children reach age 15.<sup id="cite_ref-worst_223-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worst-223">[221]</a></sup> In 2010, 74.1 per cent of children age 5 to 14 years were attending school.<sup id="cite_ref-worst_223-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worst-223">[221]</a></sup> The primary school completion rate was 80.8 per cent in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-worst_223-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worst-223">[221]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Healthcare_in_Tanzania" title="Healthcare in Tanzania">Healthcare in Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, life expectancy at birth was 61 years.<sup id="cite_ref-who_224-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who-224">[222]</a></sup> The under-five mortality rate in 2012 was 54 per 1,000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-who_224-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who-224">[222]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternal mortality">maternal mortality</a> rate in 2013 was estimated at 410 per 100,000 live births.<sup id="cite_ref-who_224-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-who-224">[222]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Premature_death" class="mw-redirect" title="Premature death">Prematurity</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a> were tied in 2010 as the leading cause of death in children under 5 years old.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO_World_Health_Statistics_2013_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_World_Health_Statistics_2013-225">[223]</a></sup> The other leading causes of death for these children were, in decreasing order, <a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">malaria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diarrhoea" class="mw-redirect" title="Diarrhoea">diarrhoea</a>, HIV, and <a href="/wiki/Measles" title="Measles">measles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WHO_World_Health_Statistics_2013_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WHO_World_Health_Statistics_2013-225">[223]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Malaria in Tanzania causes death and disease and has a "huge economic impact".<sup id="cite_ref-Progress_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Progress-226">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 13</span></sup> There were approximately 11.5&nbsp;million cases of clinical malaria in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Progress_226-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Progress-226">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 12</span></sup> In 2007–08, malaria prevalence among children aged 6 months to 5 years was highest in the <a href="/wiki/Kagera_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Kagera Region">Kagera Region</a> (41.1 per cent) on the western shore of Lake Victoria and lowest in the <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Region" title="Arusha Region">Arusha Region</a> (0.1 per cent).<sup id="cite_ref-Progress_226-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Progress-226">[224]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 12</span></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the 2010 <i>Tanzania Demographic and Health Survey 2010</i>, 15 per cent of Tanzanian women had undergone <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> (FGM)<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_205-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-205">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 295</span></sup> and 72 per cent of Tanzanian men had been circumcised.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_205-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-205">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 230</span></sup> FGM is most common in the <a href="/wiki/Manyara_Region" title="Manyara Region">Manyara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dodoma_Region" title="Dodoma Region">Dodoma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arusha_Region" title="Arusha Region">Arusha</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Singida_Region" title="Singida Region">Singida</a> regions and nonexistent in <a href="/wiki/Zanzibar" title="Zanzibar">Zanzibar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_205-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-205">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 296</span></sup> The prevalence of male circumcision was above 90 per cent in the eastern<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[225]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam_Region" class="mw-redirect" title="Dar es Salaam Region">Dar es Salaam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pwani_Region" title="Pwani Region">Pwani</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Morogoro_Region" title="Morogoro Region">Morogoro</a> regions), northern (<a href="/wiki/Kilimanjaro_Region" title="Kilimanjaro Region">Kilimanjaro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tanga_Region" title="Tanga Region">Tanga</a>, Arusha, and Manyara regions), and central areas (Dodoma and <a href="/wiki/Singida_Region" title="Singida Region">Singida</a> regions) and below 50 per cent only in the southern highlands zone (<a href="/wiki/Mbeya_Region" title="Mbeya Region">Mbeya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iringa_Region" title="Iringa Region">Iringa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rukwa_Region" title="Rukwa Region">Rukwa</a> regions).<sup id="cite_ref-DHS_205-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DHS-205">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>pages 6, 230</span></sup> </p>
      <p>2012 data showed that 53 per cent of the population used improved drinking water sources (defined as a source that "by nature of its construction and design, is likely to protect the source from outside contamination, in particular from faecal matter") and 12 per cent used improved sanitation facilities (defined as facilities that "likely hygienically separates human excreta from human contact" but not including facilities shared with other households or open to public use).<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[226]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_Tanzania" title="Women in Tanzania">Women in Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Women and men have equality before the law.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> The government signed the <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_the_Elimination_of_All_Forms_of_Discrimination_against_Women" class="mw-redirect" title="Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women">Convention on the Elimination of All Forms of Discrimination against Women</a> (CEDAW) in 1985.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> Nearly 3 out of ten females reported having experienced <a href="/wiki/Sexual_violence" title="Sexual violence">sexual violence</a> before the age of 18. <sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> The prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a> has decreased.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> School girls are reinstated back to school after delivery.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> The Police Force administration strives to separate the Gender Desks from normal police operations to enhance confidentiality of the processing of women victims of abuse.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> Most of the abuses and violence against women and children occurs at the family level.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Tanzania" title="Constitution of Tanzania">Constitution of Tanzania</a> requires that women to constitute at least 30% of all elected members of <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_(Tanzania)" title="National Assembly (Tanzania)">National Assembly</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> The gender differences in education and training have implications later in life of these women and girls.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> Unemployment is higher for females than for males.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> The right of a female employee to <a href="/wiki/Maternity_leave" class="mw-redirect" title="Maternity leave">maternity leave</a> is guaranteed in labour law.<sup id="cite_ref-cedaw_229-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cedaw-229">[227]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Tanzania" title="Culture of Tanzania">Culture of Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Judith_Wambura,.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg/220px-Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg/330px-Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg/440px-Judith_Wambura%2C.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1556" data-file-height="1037"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Judith_Wambura,.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Lady_Jaydee" title="Lady Jaydee">Judith Wambura (Lady Jaydee)</a> is a popular <a href="/wiki/Bongo_Flava" title="Bongo Flava">Bongo Flava</a> recording singer.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tanzanian_literature" title="Tanzanian literature">Tanzanian literature</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Tanzania's literary culture is primarily oral.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 68</span></sup> Major oral literary forms include folktales, poems, riddles, proverbs, and songs.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 69</span></sup> The greatest part of Tanzania's recorded oral literature is in Swahili, even though each of the country's languages has its own oral tradition.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>pages 68–9</span></sup> The country's oral literature has been declining because of the breakdown of the multigenerational social structure, making transmission of oral literature more difficult, and because increasing modernisation has been accompanied by the devaluation of oral literature.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 69</span></sup> </p>
      <p>Books in Tanzania are often expensive and hard to come by.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 75</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Doling_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-230">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 16</span></sup> Most Tanzanian literature is in Swahili or English.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>page 75</span></sup> Major figures in Tanzanian written literature include <a href="/wiki/Shaaban_Robert" class="mw-redirect" title="Shaaban Robert">Shaaban Robert</a> (considered the father of Swahili literature), Muhammed Saley Farsy, Faraji Katalambulla, Adam Shafi Adam, <a href="/wiki/Muhammed_Said_Abdulla" title="Muhammed Said Abdulla">Muhammed Said Abdalla</a>, Said Ahmed Mohammed Khamis, Mohamed Suleiman Mohamed, <a href="/wiki/Euphrase_Kezilahabi" title="Euphrase Kezilahabi">Euphrase Kezilahabi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Ruhumbika" title="Gabriel Ruhumbika">Gabriel Ruhumbika</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ebrahim_Hussein" title="Ebrahim Hussein">Ebrahim Hussein</a>, <a href="/wiki/May_Balisidya" title="May Balisidya">May Materru Balisidya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fadhy_Mtanga" title="Fadhy Mtanga">Fadhy Mtanga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Abdulrazak_Gurnah" title="Abdulrazak Gurnah">Abdulrazak Gurnah</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Penina_Muhando" title="Penina Muhando">Penina O. Mlama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>pages 76–8</span></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Amani-TT4798.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Amani-TT4798.jpg/220px-Amani-TT4798.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Amani-TT4798.jpg/330px-Amani-TT4798.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Amani-TT4798.jpg/440px-Amani-TT4798.jpg 2x" data-file-width="515" data-file-height="520"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Amani-TT4798.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A <a href="/wiki/Tingatinga_(painting)" title="Tingatinga (painting)">Tingatinga</a> painting
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Painting_and_sculpture">Painting and sculpture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Painting and sculpture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Two Tanzanian art styles have achieved international recognition.<sup id="cite_ref-Doling_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-230">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 17</span></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tingatinga_(painting)" title="Tingatinga (painting)">Tingatinga</a> school of painting, founded by <a href="/wiki/Edward_Said_Tingatinga" class="mw-redirect" title="Edward Said Tingatinga">Edward Said Tingatinga</a>, consists of brightly coloured enamel paintings on canvas, generally depicting people, animals, or daily life.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 113</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Doling_230-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-230">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 17</span></sup> After Tingatinga's death in 1972, other artists adopted and developed his style, with the genre now being the most important tourist-oriented style in East Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-Otiso_196-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Otiso-196">[194]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 113</span></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Doling_230-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-230">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 17</span></sup> </p>
      <p>Historically, there were limited opportunities for formal European art training in Tanzania and many aspiring Tanzanian artists left the country to pursue their vocation.<sup id="cite_ref-Doling_230-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Doling-230">[228]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>p. 17</span></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Tanzania" title="Sport in Tanzania">Sport in Tanzania</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tanzania_National_Main_Stadium_Aerial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tanzania_National_Main_Stadium_Aerial.jpg/220px-Tanzania_National_Main_Stadium_Aerial.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tanzania_National_Main_Stadium_Aerial.jpg/330px-Tanzania_National_Main_Stadium_Aerial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/Tanzania_National_Main_Stadium_Aerial.jpg/440px-Tanzania_National_Main_Stadium_Aerial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3490" data-file-height="2034"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tanzania_National_Main_Stadium_Aerial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/National_Stadium_(Tanzania)" title="National Stadium (Tanzania)">National Stadium</a> in <a href="/wiki/Dar_es_Salaam" title="Dar es Salaam">Dar es Salaam</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is very popular throughout the country.<sup id="cite_ref-Wairagala_231-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wairagala-231">[229]</a></sup> The most popular <a href="/wiki/Tanzanian_Premier_League" title="Tanzanian Premier League">professional football clubs</a> in Dar es Salaam are the <a href="/wiki/Young_Africans_F.C." class="mw-redirect" title="Young Africans F.C.">Young Africans F.C.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simba_S.C." title="Simba S.C.">Simba S.C.</a><sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[230]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Tanzania_Football_Federation" title="Tanzania Football Federation">Tanzania Football Federation</a> is the governing body for football in the country. </p>
      <p>Other popular sports include <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a>, boxing, <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">volleyball</a>, <a href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" class="mw-redirect" title="Athletics (sport)">athletics</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Wairagala_231-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wairagala-231">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[231]</a></sup> The National Sports Council also known as Baraza la Michezo la Taifa is the governing body for sports in the country under the Ministry of Information, Youth, Sports and Culture.<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">[232]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinema">Cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Tanzania&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Tanzania has a popular film industry known as "Bongo Movie". The music industry is known as "<a href="/wiki/Bongo_Flava" title="Bongo Flava">Bongo Flava</a>" which is in itself also a niche genre of music in Tanzania. </p>
